Honestly, while I respect the effort in this animation, the result feels quite inaccurate when you deeply analyze both characters based on their actual abilities and lore.  Alex Mercer is biologically superior to Cole MacGrath in almost every way:  Mercer can regenerate from almost any form of damage, including full dismemberment and even a nuclear bomb. His healing factor is borderline absurd.  His offensive capabilities are far more versatile: claws, blade arms, hammerfists, tendrils, biomass projectiles, groundspikes, shield, armor, and the ability to consume any biological target instantly.  He's much stronger physically, able to toss tanks, rip helicopters apart, and blitz enemies at superhuman speeds.  Cole, on the other hand:  Is limited by his electrical energy reserve. If drained, he's extremely vulnerable.  While he can generate very destructive attacks (like Ionic Storms, Lightning Tornado, etc), they require charge buildup and are mostly long-range.  His durability, while above normal humans, is nowhere close to Mercer's regenerative feats.  Cole has no "consume" or "energy absorption" ability that would let him steal Mercer's powers or biomass. That scene in the video where Cole somehow pulls Mercerâ€™s biomass in is completely fabricated â€” that ability simply does not exist in the inFamous lore.  The major issue with this animation:  It heavily nerfs Alex Mercerâ€™s aggression and regeneration while giving Cole non-canon abilities.  In a realistic fight, Mercer would close the distance quickly and force a brutal close-combat scenario where Cole's ranged advantage becomes almost useless.  Best case scenario for Cole:  He lands an incredibly powerful, fully charged Ionic Storm or similar attack early in the fight before Mercer can get close. Even then, Alex may regenerate unless completely vaporized.  Realistically: Mercer takes the win 8/10 times due to overwhelming regeneration, offensive variety, strength, durability, and close-range dominance.  Bottom line: Fun animation, but the scaling here doesnâ€™t do justice to how absurdly broken Alex Mercer really is.  If we ever got a canon inFamous vs Prototype crossover, itâ€™d be brutal.

Prototype 2 ruined the fledgling franchise.  They turned Alex from an anti-hero to a full blown supervillain.  No one liked the 180 change, the new protagonist was just basically Alex 2.0 so the sales tanked.  DB rarely makes mistakes but they made some here.  Saying the blacklight virus "only" works down to DNA so Cole would resist, is unfounded.  DNA controls what you are, change it by 2% and you're a chimp.  So it would NOT be reasonable to assume Cole would be resistant to ALL viruses, especially not one as virulent as blacklight.  If Cole's DNA was altered, well he wouldn't BE Cole anymore.  Cole's draining ability drains neural electricity, which is BETWEEN neurons NOT inside cells themselves.  So that "advantage" is inapplicable here.  Mind control powers =/= blacklight infection.  A viral infection is not "physically altering" as they implied.  Viruses basically use the cells to reproduce, it's not like blacklight is killing a cell and replacing it.  So Cole resisting blacklight again is unfounded.  DB also ignored how Alex could easily dodge cannon shells and survive a nuke.  Oh and he's resistant to electricity.  The Actual Winner... Alex Mercer.

Death Battles are the equivalent of anime fights without the unnecessary dialog.
These are some of my favorite game-characters of all times and frankly i was incredibly excited to hear that these two would fight one another.  These two had a lot things to speak about, both in terms of abilities, power and experience. Both had a lot of weapons/abilities to throw at each, both had healing factors, enormous level of destructional abilities and both could absorb people and they have taken down hundreds if thousands of armed militias and monsters alike.    Alex Mercer as a former scientist, were by default a lot smarter than cole and seemingly also held a lot more experience. Especially if we consider all of the memories and abilities Mercer had absorbed, in terms of both intellect and abilities. Not to mention he was also a great tactician that had fooled both the Military and the Gentech co. and had even infiltrated their ranks several times. He was also stronger in pure physic thanks to the virus and all the people he absorbed that included soldiers, infected people and other monsters in general. Not to mention thanks to his many deadly close-range weapons and stronger physic meant that he most likely had the  close-range combat in the bag. His black tendrils also could drag Cole Closer of just throw him around, which would make it harder for Cole to focus and counter-attack probably. His healing factor was also quite broken, since he could recover from just a piece of flesh after being nuked by a bomb. And unlike Cole, Mercer also did not need to absorb things to restock on power. So Mercer could even win if he could hold the fight on for long enough. So with all that said and done, Mercer definitely had a couple of things that could put Cole in a difficult situation. Unfortunately though that's where cole starts to take the lead.  Cole wasn't nearly as strong Mercer in pure strength, but he had lot of other things that mercer couldn`t counter so easily. Cole overall had a lot more control in this battle thanks to his stronger versatility alone. Cole could also trap Mercer in Ice and even in that black gooey(good power and evil power) and that alone would make it hard for Mercer to escape, especially since viruses have a tendency to work less efficient under extreme cold temperatures. While Mercer held the advantage in close combat, it didn't not mean that cole didn't have ways around it. Cole could use his amp to defend himself, use his lightning lightsaber on his arms to fight coles-range and even just protect himself with force fields, which Mercer did not really have an out to. Even Mercers tendrils could potentially be electrocuted or frozen completely if it came into contact with cole. He could also simply also just force Mercer back with tornadoes, lightning strikes and his big ice technique that could freeze a whole city block. While Mercers healing factor was superior to Cole`s healing factor, but that did not make him invincible. Even if we take the power-scaling aside, Mercers healing abilities could only do so much after a prolonged battle. Like his Battle against James Heller, where Mercer had absorsed his other infected comrades right before the fight and got a major boost. But even with that, he still lost against Heller. That at least shows even with a power boost, his healing factor did not improve so much that it would tip the scale. With that in mind and considering that all of Cole`s arsenal could hurt Mercer, it just seems a bit unlikely that Mercer would come on top. Especially since Cole had a clear advantage in fire power and range attacks. That combined with Cole`s better speed stats and power, Mercer would simply just have a hard time winning this fight.  Despite all these amazing facts about these two characters, they are somehow still human to some extent and both can still get harmed by most attacks in their opponents arsenal(even with their healing factors). Cole could potentially get pummeled down or skewed by Mercers weapons and Mercer could get fried or frozen down by Cole`s abilities. With that in mind and the fact that neither of them a had a definitive counter against each other meant that it came down to power and durability in the long run especially since both have survived enormous level of destruction. But according to the stats shown at least in this video Cole just comes out on top in the end          Mercer`s intelligent, superior strength and better healing abilities certainly gave cole a tough fight of the century, but Cole`s stronger versatility, better speed stats and greater power eventually settled this fight for good.

We only saw half of Alex Mercer's powers
In a gameplay sense, Alex has *WAAAAY* better in-game durability feats and somewhat more effective close combat weapons (even with the amp, which is better than the lightning blades), as well as solidly better mobility feats than any playable version of Cole with the possible exception of the Halloween special vampire Cole using his bat swarm ability, and that's more limited in its use than Alex's movement powers. On the other hand, though, Cole has *WAAAAY* better long-range damage output and a few solid range-control tools, backed up by functionally unbeatable defense against everything Alex can do at range if he can maintain distance. If you based this battle on gameplay instead of lore (which you shouldn't, just to be clear, but if you did...) then the fight would come down to a couple of major factors.  If the "fight" starts with Alex arriving in Cole's city, with Cole not knowing he's coming and Alex unaware of Cole's presence, it's an easy win for Alex. Because at some point, Alex either sees Cole and realises "dude's done up like a hero" and he's got the tactical knowledge to study a potentially powerful opponent before attacking, or consumes a random at some point and learns from doing so that Cole exists and has superpowers, and does more research. Then disguises himself as a civilian until he's walking past Cole, and suddenly shanks him with claws or cuts him in half with a blade and game over. Gameplay Cole has a pretty pathetic health pool and a few quick hits would cut him down before he could respond, and his shield doesn't stop melee attackers.  If Cole shows up where Alex lives instead, and both know each other's reputations and a bit about their powerset, Alex has much less of an advantage, *BUT* if he's smart - which he is - there's a good chance of him trying to sneak up on Cole. This probably won't work *FULLY* because Cole's bioelectric sensor pulse is likely to register Alex as being something different from a normal human, but it'll still get him closer than Cole would like before the fight starts. At this point, it's a gamble on whether Cole's able to stall and play keepaway for long enough to end Alex's healthbar or not before they get into stabbity range. This one could easily go either way, but because Cole has a few explosive tricks and loses less of his mobility while using his shield power, I think he's got a bit of an edge here... as long as there's some nearby wires to grind on.  If the fight is engaged with both fighters becoming aware of each other at longer range (say, for example, Alex getting spotted in armour form, or caught consuming someone), then it's solidly in Cole's favour, with the range advantage being both offensive and defensive - his HP isn't any higher at range, but his shield means it doesn't need to be, and his firepower is more reliable and versatile than Alex can bring to the party while rivalling the heaviest hits Alex could send his way in return. He's got abilities which could stall Alex long enough to negate the HP advantage, and interrupt attempts to flee as well, so it doesn't even turn into a stalemate.  All that said, my biggest problem with the video's lore-based analysis is that you point to Alex needing to weaken his enemies to consume them when that's not entirely true, and don't bring up the same weakness for Cole when it's significantly more true for him. Alex has stealth consume skills which can allow him to eat any human and even some superhuman opponents if he can avoid being recognised prior to the attack. Even when it's true for Alex, many enemies he can consume can still be active and fighting as long as he hurts them enough, Cole specifically needs to incapacitate a target so they can't struggle free of him while he leeches their energy, and even then, a more heavily weakened enemy than the ones Alex can consume is able to put up a solid fight against Cole while he's channeling his power into the attempt at siphoning their life energy. Incapacitating normal humans is laughably easy, and even some low-level superhumans can reliably be one-shotted into a vulnerable state, but he needs a notable amount more effort to do the same to a more powerful enemy, which Alex would qualify as. Doesn't change the winner, but I don't think that particular ability is what would actually and the fight. Massive atomising sky lightning attack is a much more plausible option for a win condition.

Im sorry, but no. This deathbattle is so factually wrong it's not even funny. I'm not saying this to be a prototype fanatic, I'm telling you this is factually wrong and I can give several logical details and reasons as to why.  1. He did NOT tank the blast of the raysphere, this is a myth. While from a first glance it looks like that is the case, a major detail people are overlooking is that the ground he was laying on was completely unburnt,even still having the yellow driving paint. This implies that the raysphere had a built in field or barrier that would protect the user from the force of the blast. When Kessler said he was worried Cole wouldn't survive the blast, he was referring to the fact that the raysphere was a rushed and malfunctioning prototype known to kill the user. The actual damage he took from the raysphere malfunction was more on the lvl of a grenade blowing up in his face. Impressive, but it still massively lowers the impressiveness of this feat. If Cole can't survive a direct hit from an RPG, there's no way in Hell he took a nuclear lvl blast head on. While Alex wasn't at the center of his nuke, he didn't have to be. The nuke was designed to wipe not just the city and infected, but was also designed to desintegrate the entire land mass of New York. He was still in the radius of this bomb and yet a piece of him was still able to survive that on top of the radiation damage that piece without a doubt would have taken. You bring up how the beasts explosion was larger than that of the p1 nuke, but this is pointless info as Cole wasn't anywhere near the radius of that explosion, he was unconscious on a boat half way to new murray.  2. Cole being immune to Sasha's power is only half true. While yes he was shown completely immune to her mind control ability of her tar, he still suffered adverse effects from it such as Sasha being able to communicate to him via a telepathic link, she was able to make him hallucinate giant reapers that could do physical damage to him, and direct contact with the tar effected his biology causing him to have a lower energy capacity. If he can be that badly effected by a conduit power despite being one of the more powerful conduits, then he cant possibly be immune to the effects of blacklight as the virus has been known to cause cannibalistic madness, bodily mutation, and organ failure in so cases.  And for people who are gonna bring up the empire city plague, that wasn't a virus. It wasn't even a disease, it was the result of people getting sick from rayfield radiation exposure which all conduits are immune to. It's not because he was immune to disease. There's nothing to suggest he ever was. Him being immune to disease is a baseless claim with nothing supporting it other than he didn't catch anything in his 2 only games.  3. You talk about how he beat the beast after using the RFI like it was a feat, it's not. Saying that he was on par with the beast because he used the RFI is literally the equivalent of saying Batman is on par with Superman because he brought kryptonite. You don't get it, the beast wasn't just some op conduit, it was on the lvl of nigh-omnipotence. When cole and Zeke hit it with a tsar Bomb direct hit, it merely gathered it's scattered ray field particles and put itself back together. In the final fight, it walked through a large naval force on top of a city filled with both militia and laroaches men on top of both Cole and nix both being powerhouse conduits. Neither man nor Conduit could harm it in anyway. It was only once Cole started using the RFI's energy that the beast finally started showing signs of slowing down and weakness. This isn't a feat, because it wasn't Cole's normal energy he was firing at. If you take the evil route, Nix has been shown to be able to weaken and almost kill the beast with the RFI, meaning anyone with the RFI can do this, not just Cole, but anyone conduit or not.  4. Cole fighting more dangerous opponents again is only half true. The most dangerous opponent he's ever face  not counting the beast isn't even Kessler, it's alden. He was capable of lifting metal regardless of it's weight with the power of his mind. Alden was far more powerful than Cole, Cole even admits as much upon their first meet. The only reason Cole won against Alden was because as Kessler said, he had squandered his potential. He could have just chucked the nearest bus at Cole and Cole wouldn't be able to stop it, instead, he creates a giant metallic construct he pilot to fight. Which gives Cole a fighting chance.  As for Kessler. He's not as strong as your making him out to be. Unlike Cole, Kessler wasn't at the center of his raysphere explosion, meaning Cole was far stronger, he put up such a good fight though because he's far more experienced with his power with cole. Cole had only a few weeks with his power during the time whereas Kessler had several decades. If time would have allowed it, Cole would have eventually developed the exact same abilities as Kessler only even more powerful.  5. Your wording on Cole's bioleech make you sound like your being purely hypothetical and dont know if his bioleech would actually interfere with mercers regeneration or not. You not even taking into account the amount of mass mercer would have and there for not taking into consideration how much energy he would contain. Every person Cole ever bioleeched was either human lvl with human mass, and conduits with human mass. He's never done it to someone like mercer who has enough mass to cover an entire city. Cole takes longer to drain an energy source the more energy the source has, logic would dictate this to be the case for biological beings as well. This is all assuming Alex would even give him the chance to pull it off. He struggle doing it to an older weaker version of himself. There's no way he'd with a physical struggle against a guy who can throw an apc with 1 hand  6. This is something you actually failed to bring up when talking about Cole, and that is blackouts and water are his greatest weaknesses. Water fries him and a blackout makes him physically weaker as he even states. The second mercer sees Cole absorbing electricity, Alex is gonna immediately connect the dots and either go for the main power grid to destroy it or simply cut Cole's arms off. Don't tell me he wouldn't figure it out. Anyone could figure out that an electric guys would get his power from electricity     I could continue on forever but I think I made my self clear this video is wrong  I like Cole too guys, I like him personality wise far more than mercer. Mercer is a sociopath who only cares about his sister whereas  Cole cares about everyone. You fellas most likely have one or two comments like these picking apart your videos or trying to do your job better than you. I am not trying to disreguard the work you do or what timeframe you have to accomplish it or say that the end result of this video was poor, esoecially considering it was an old format script from years ago. So, getting into the meat of the matter, here's a detailed explonation of why I think this fight could have gone differently. Overall you did a fantastic job, way more thorough than I can accomplish as of writing this comment but you did overlook some bery key details about Alex, particularly his experience and creativity.  Resonably speaking  and as an overview for this whole comment in case ya don't want to read the full explination.  Coles abilities are largely dependant on some sorce of energy, while Alex is only dependant on some source of bio organic material to heal injuries and supply his MOST devistating powers. Alex has a greater wealth of knowledge than Cole could ever collect in his time scanning the recent memories of people and Coles major reliance on his Comduit powers.   Alex does not need to recharge his wider variety of powers, the critical mass abilities being the only acception. On the other hand when Cole uses any kind of intense ability, electricity grenades for example, there is a significant drop in his stored charge. Without a steady source of power Cole would eventually run out of power while Alex would still be able to fight very easily, even if cole could still use ice that would only help him temporarily as those powers still require some electricity from what I recall. I could easily be mistaken, though even with access to ice without a drain on his stored charge Alex can easily move out of the way or even counter those attacks. At the very least Alex woukd simply be able to jump above the ice.   Alex has consumed at least a few hundred people, many of which are military commandos with training, not to menion all the civilians who could have any number of memories on self defense or aggresive training. With the memories of all the people Alex has consumed he could create several different faccimilies of fighting styles ALL of which could cripple someone in a one on one fight. My understanding of conduits is that they aren't that physically remarkable when you take away their powers apart from their regenerstion factor which in Coles' case can being him back from death though only if his body remains largely in one piece, we have yet to see an example of a conduit surviving decapitstion which theoretically Alex could do.  Most likely, the minute Alex encountered Cole and they had their initial clash Alex would be able to understand they are equals in terms of abilities. Although Alex's arsenal is largely close quarters he still has the ability to deceive cole, all Alex would need is a single moment when Cole couldnt see him to choose a disguise from the multitude he would have access too in order to fool Cole into trusting or wanting to help him and long story short consume Cole. Alex does not need to wear down a human to consume them and even if Cole is more durable because of his ability to regenerate this could be completely negated if Alex were to break Coles neck. Cole is able to bring himself back from a lot but the major problem is that it takes time, once Cole is down for the count Alex could consume him. Even with a regeneration factor matching the consumption of biomass it would be an eventual loss for Cole, his body would be trying to repair the damage of a broken neck and severed nervosystem while the infection of blacklight would be draining his bodies resources and ultimately win the battle of cellular attrition.  But let's say Cole could heal in time to escape consumption, having learned Alex can disguise himself and will try to incapacitate him first. Alex most likely would have had time to extract some of Coles genetic memory, and thus memories or how Coles electro and crio kinesis work and what is needed to power them. Keep in mind Alex is capable of running indefinitely while carrying a fully grown person. If Alex can get ahold of Cole in any way and get them both away from a power grid Cole would be finished, unable to juice up like he could normally. Even by draining the bioelectricity of living things it would be a far weaker yield than he's used too, while Alex doesnt need his food to be alive to use their biomass.   Ultimately the deciding factor of the whole fight would be Alex's greater wealth of experience, and Coles dependance on external sources of power to fuel his abilities.  If you've gotten this far, thank you for reading. Please note im not an expert and I may have missed several things or not taken something into account, like how Cole can akso extract memories, theoretically given enough time Cole could balance his physical skill with his conduit powers. But, Alex can process memories AND experience in way less time, and effectively use the information. They are both op characters, and the guys on DB can only think about a matchup for so long before they need to invest time in another project. Ultimately tjis video was extremely mentally stimulating, two unstoppable forces who can effectively battle for a long time in the right circumstances especially in the right environment. Thank you Wizz and bolmstick for making your content, flawed as it might be. And I eagerly await the responses of anyone determined to get this far in my comment, best wishes  - The Wanderer

Another thing in Cole's favor. Those who played or at least watched the endings of Infamous 2 know that Cole was empowered by the RFI in the good ending, however from what we know the RFI's ability is primarily the opposite, that of weakening a conduit. We also know that the Beast drained Cole's powers at the end of their first confrontation, and because of that Cole was weaker than in the prologue throughout the entire game, only towards the end of the game did his powers finally surpass their original level.  With this comes my theory, since the Beast is basically a walking Ray Sphere and RFI absorbs "Ray Field Energy", when RFI was fully charged it started absorbing that energy to a small degree. In the process this absorbed the "Beast's energy" that was preventing Cole from accessing/returning his full power. You can notice that at the beginning when Cole prepares for combat and sometimes just by moving he releases electricity, something that stops happening after he has been drained.  What I mean is, the power that was "given" by the RFI is simply *Cole's TRUE POWER*.

I think reading into the Ray Sphere's destructive power is a little misguided -- Kessler might not have been certain Cole would survive it, but that might be better chalked up to not being sure if there were any quirks because of time travel. While it tore apart the Beast's human body (when destroyed), I always assumed it had more to do with his eventual resulting powerset, i.e. his cellular stuff. Notably, it didn't tear apart Bertrand (who was at ground zero of another activation) or Nix (who was very nearby). Neither of which had anywhere close to the durability assumed of Cole -- Nix shooting herself like a bullet at Beast and killing herself only stunned him. Ray Spheres seem to only "activate" anyone with a Conduit gene, and kill anyone without one.   Moreover, the Beast was only killable through a combo of Cole channeling an extreme amount of power through the RFI, after which he used it to kill the Beast -- conventional damage didn't seem to be a possible method of killing the Beast, since he didn't just regenerate from a single cell. He regenerated from like... literally nothing. He was a consciousness without a body. Cole never hit that level of power without distinct external factors.  The Beast wasn't even trying to KILL Cole for most of their fight. Just get rid of the RFI.  Moreover, I don't know why they'd bring up Alex needing to weaken someone for an absorption where I don't recall Cole ever biodraining someone that wasn't literally stuck to the floor, i.e. someone he'd straight up beaten. As minor nitpicks, while Cole did resist Sasha's tar, he was not unaffected by it, moreover, are we saying Alex's ability to corrupt is only as strong as Sasha? It's probably stronger. Also, Alex can start absorbing Cole's biomass anytime he touches him, even with an attack, even his blade attack. Any of those moments he struck or held Cole he could spend absorbing him. Also, the Beast never used that super strong attack against Cole. Output matching durability really only is a thing for physical contact. So it works for Mercer who is all physicality, but Cole is more questionable. Which brings his durability and output in to question since the same applies to The Beast. We have plenty of emitters who put this concept to the test in real life. Most emitters cannot withstand the same beating they dish out. They're just not structured for it. Does a grenade output more force than an axe? Yes, but can an axe destroy a grenade? Also, yes. Yet, when Heller had Alex at his mercy, he realized he *did* succeed in making someone like him. Better yet, someone *better* than him. Unlike Alex, who had no reason to maintain his humanity, Heller still did. If Alex was the Prototype, Heller was the finished product.  "Welcome to top of the food chain" isn't meant to be rude, or even a compliment, it's a warning. Heller is going to be alone, like Alex was. He can try to fill that void with family and friends like Alex tried to, but even if Heller's family accepts him, he will likely outlive his own children and likely even grandchildren. He is at the top, and Alex could not be de-throned until something stronger came along. The same will likely happen to Heller. (Or would've if Prototype wasn't cancelled...)

I find your reasoning on this one underwhelming. First of all, gravity is not electromagnetic in nature.   I found your evaluation of Cole optimistic. The calculation you used for Cole's power limit was a major extrapolation with little to back it up. Let's assume that Cole can disintegrate bullets and harvest some energy from the process. That might imply being able to convert some of the mass into energy, but doesn't tell you anything about the efficiency or his upper limit on power output. You need to look at his actual power output, not assume that he perfectly converts mass into energy and is able to harvest and utilize all of it. Further, it looks like he can do this to bullets, but can he do it to people? If not, it's basically a moot point. Further, aside from the shield, you didn't mention any defensive or healing abilities. If he doesn't have any and Mercer hurts him, he basically dies. The way you talk about his ability to reroute electricity implies that he can move (or at least use his powers) at 90% of the speed of light, but that's not born out by the rest of the context I've seen for the character. It makes more sense that he sensed a current and was able to redirect it with human reaction speed, and the game just showed it in a fanciful way. Now, to be fair, I know less about Infamous than Prototype, so it's possible that I'm missing something, but you didn't present a compelling case for Cole's powers being even remotely close to the scale that you claimed that they were.  Looking at Mercer, it's a pretty small extrapolation to say that he must have an enormous amount of mass. He can consume hundreds of people and remain the same size, plus he can grow giant spikes and tentacles. If we apply conservation of mass, he could easily weight many metric tons. That implies that even if Cole is able to convert mass into energy, it's not at a fast enough rate to protect him from Mercer. Claiming that Cole can use this capability to kill Mercer quickly is a dubious claim. Mercer can be shot by tanks and assault helicopters, and it doesn't even phase him. He'll take a little damage, eat someone, and walk it off. He can run down a street filled with cars and knock the cars out of his way like a battering ram through Styrofoam. He shouldn't be particularly inconvenienced by Cole's ice powers.   Just based on comparing the gameplay of the games, I'm skeptical that Cole could survive getting attacked by Mercer, and I have trouble seeing how Cole could seriously hurt Mercer unless Mercer stood there passively for 5 minutes, and that's assuming that you're right that Cole can disintegrate him given enough time. You've tentatively sold me on the Ray Sphere being able to kill Mercer, not on Cole being able to do it.

Wow, you clearly don't know how to science correctly despite how much science you try and back your theories with.   Cellular regeneration on Alex's level makes him impossible to destroy, because according to scientific theory "Matter can neither be created, nor completely destroyed, merely transferred to another form". This is the very reason why being consumed at the end of Prototype 2 was the only true way to ensure he was gone for good.  Not only does Cole lack the capability to generate enough power to completely eliminate all of Alex's cells (I refer you to Perfect Cell who has the same regenerative ability, and Gohan had to pack enough power into a Kamehameha for it to EXTEND MILES INTO SPACE to do him in, a power scale Cole is nowhere close to), that last attack basically ensured his failure. Do you know what an explosion does to organic tissue? It scatters it, across a very wide area. It doesn't matter how much of Alex's regeneration Cole tried to 'sap' with that move beforehand, that explosive finish just pushed Alex's biological material all over the place.   All Cole did was prolong the inevitable, ensuring that not only will Alex come back - after absorbing a crow, a dog, a person, hell, even a *fly* would be enough to start (because he is not just Perfect Cell, he is Perfect Cell fused with John Carpenter's 'The Thing') . . . but there will probably be *multiple* Alex Mercers created once the disparate parts of his cellular anatomy absorbs enough biomass to regenerate as individual copies.   This is almost exactly like how you guys flubbed the Guts v. Nightmare battle by ignoring a huge part of Soul Calibur canon: It didn't matter if Guts was strong enough to kill Nightmare's physical body, because he didn't use Soul Calibur, the only weapon that can actually destroy the essence of Soul Edge which is the very reason Nightmare exists at all, and even then, only if enough force is used to completely destroy both weapons, because as long as one exists, the other will return.  Cole loses. End of story.

I've played both of these games and I have to say I was surprised to see how this turned out.  I thought that Alex's edge of close range, enhanced mobility, and regeneration would do Cole in.  Cole can heal himself but only by draining an electrical source. He could regenerate with the help of a storm, but that's more situational than overall. The Polarity Shield can give Cole more energy from blocking projectiles, but I don't remember if it could heal him at the same time. Cole's mobility is only enhanced through electrical items like wires, and the Static Thrusters don't really give him much more than gliding while Alex had enhanced running speed, can jump to incredible heights, wall run and glide by expelling biomass from his body. Cole can move with the Lightning Tether, but that requires time to aim while Alex doesn't need that requirement.  Not to mention the weaknesses. Alex has only displayed weakness twice: being injected with an antibody that hindered his powers and Bloodtox, a chemical that acts as a poison to him. But these are all genetically engineered to kill the Blacklight virus, therefore it's not readily available.  While Cole has a weakness to water. Although he can stand in puddles harmless enough, if he gets soaked by a large amount of it, it can kill him. And in an urban setting with water towers and fire hydrants, Alex can hold an advantage over Cole if he can exploit that weakness.  But I forgot about the scale of the Ray Sphere's power along with The Beast's. Even The Beast mentioned regenerating itself atom by atom, if that's any indication.

I like how the outcome made sense scientifically as well. In a battle between someone who can control electricity and someone who could control biomass, the one who can control electricity will always win. Even excluding the nervous system, organic matter is mainly reliant on bioelectricity to determine shape. How would a baby in the womb know to have 4 limbs and a head in that specific fashion? Biological matter, including viruses like the Blacklight, use bioelectric signaling all the time to determine their shape and structure. Coleâ€™s ability to both manipulate and straight-up steal that electricity from Alex almost completely negates his physical form entirely, making this matchup doomed from the start.

Plus, Cole absorbing bio-electricity is not the same as Alex's consumption of DNA, so Cole couldn't "do the same thing to Alex" as described.  I also don't see the logic that Cole could resist infection because he could withstand his atoms being broken down by the Ray Sphere detonation. Infection rearranges the genes, and therefore molecules, and the Conduit gene, as described, is a gene, which is made out of molecules, so that aspect of Cole that gives him his powers is genetic, not atomic. Plus, does molecular DNA survive nukes? No, but because these are fictional characters, we let those rules slide.  Also notice that in the results, it says Cole is "Vulnerable to possible corruption" yet they explain that away right before, so why is that point even there? That point alone suggests Cole could be infected. If he could be corrupted by multiple other sources, then the Blacklight Virus should theoretically be able to work on him. Also, Alex has consumed people without "weakening" them, and infection is not the same as consumption, so that's another inaccurate point.  While I find Death Battle scaling to often be inaccurate as to what characters are actually capable of from a narrative standpoint, I can accept by their logic that Cole has better stats. But Alex's infection seems to be the number one deciding factor regardless of stats. I will admit that I am more familiar with Alex as a character, and therefore biased in Alex's favor, I don't think the reasoning shown in the episode is sufficient to give Cole the victory. Also, Bad Karma Cole is not canon, so bringing him up is going outside of canon Cole.

Squidward VS Bob From Mugen
This feels like a case of "This guy can take a punch harder than the other guy, so he must win." I don't know who would win or lose, but their explanations are subpar. Keep in mind that I only played Prototype and not Infamous, so maybe Cole has tricks up his sleeve that would guarantee a win, but even in that case, Death Battle would just be even more incompetent in explaining their reasoning. For example, they say that Cole must be stronger than Mercer, but the gameplay of Prototype isn't always one of combat. It's about tactics and consuming so much biomass that tank shells stop being a nuisance. While Cole's radar would prevent Mercer from sneaking up on him in the traditional sense, if Mercer is fighting good Cole, then all Mercer would have to do is turn into one of the civilians he munched on and get behind Cole's guard. I don't think Cole has any virus sense in his radar. Force field doesn't matter much if you're pointing it at the wrong person. It is possible that Mercer's biomass would generate more bioelectricity since he keeps eating people, but Death Battle never considers such an approach. Another thing is that it isn't confirmed in the analysis that Cole absorbs 100% of the bioelectricity. At the very least, he absorbs enough to kill someone, but if the body still has energy, then it is possible that Mercer would survive. He just needs one cell to remain alive in order to come back, something Death Battle mentions. Could Cole absorb 100% of someone's bioelectricity? If he can't take away the energy from every single cell in Mercer, then it doesn't matter. Which leads to their argument that Cole can destroy on an atomic level. True, if Cole can do this, Mercer would lose. However, the examples they gave in the analysis suggest that Cole can target atomic structures but has not disintegrated anybody down to their last atom. Is Cole capable of destroying every cell, or can he only target specific structures?  Lastly, they mention that Mercer has to weaken someone before he can absorb them, and this is completely false. He has to weaken those infected with the virus to absorb them. But humans he can consume after grabbing them, which is why the human boss battles are usually the human in a tank or helicopter, requiring Mercer to beat up the vehicle first, or surrounded by threats, so Mercer has to sneak upon them. Cole could be absorbed the moment Mercer got within slapping distance.  Death Battle does argue that Cole can resist the virus, so Cole isn't in danger when Mercer is that close, but their explanation is nonsensical. Their argument is essentially, "Cole survived atomic damage, therefore he can resist the virus." But these are two different things. Viruses don't eradicate people on an atomic level. They hijack cells and force them to replicate more viruses. If Cole had the power to manipulate his atoms, sure, he could then just manipulate his atoms against the virus. But Death Battle's claim that "because Cole survived a nuke, he can survive anything" makes no sense. He may survive being ripped apart, but having your cells turn into virus factories are completely different.  Honestly, this is the reason why I don't watch Death Battle that much anymore. I can't help myself whenever I see a fight that I would love, but I keep leaving disappointed. If they're going to do this much research and put this much thought into the battle, they can at least put some effort into making sure what they say makes sense.

I'm amazed anyone was thinking about these characters! I've always felt that Prototype had such a good foundation to its story, but was rather wasted on the game that ended up being made. For once, I'd like to see an edgy character done right in more media rather than keep seeing Shadow the Hedgehog copycats.
Shulk from Xenoblade Chronicles vs Erin Yeager from Attack on Titan  It sounds random at first, but the more you start thinking about it, the more you see the parallels in those two.   Both are trapped in a small place at the start of their stories just waiting to be slaughtered, wanting nothing more than to break down the walls to find something greater and save humanity. They both inherit these godlike abilities/weapons to destroy these massive previously undefeatable foes.  Both can see into the future, but while one of them changes the future, the other is bound to its inevitability.  By the end for them, Shulk could wipe out a man capable of destroying his world with the help of two titans and Erin could destroy all of humanity... singlehandedly

As for the next one, I was shocked to see its going to be Frieza vs Megatron, one I've been wanting to see them do. Now this is actually trickier than one thinks. It really depends on the versions they use (like if they do one specific megatron or a composite and/or if they include Heroes feats for Frieza). Frieza probably wins most outcomes, but there are versions of Megatron that could kill Frieza. First of all, most, if not all versions, of Megatron at his base power are capable of surviving planet busting attacks (One time he took multiple hits of said strength from Unicron, the literal transformers devil), so he can hold his own against Frieza and maybe Golden Frieza. There are versions of Megatron that use darkmatter or dark energon that kill organics, which could bypass Frieza's durability. And if we include his stronger forms like Galvatron, then it gets trickier.  And if they use Alternity Megatron's ultimate form, then its a clear stomp for Megatron because at that point, Megs is a multiversal destroyer.
